If any of the\n29: # properties are modified, applications should be restarted to ensure the\n30: # changes are properly reflected.\n31: #\n32: # The special \"include\" property can be defined one or multiple times with\n33: # a filesystem path value. The effect of each definition is to include a\n34: # referred security properties file inline, adding all its properties.\n35: # Security properties defined before an include statement may be overridden\n36: # by properties in the included file, if their names match. Conversely,\n37: # properties defined after an include statement may override properties in\n38: # the included file.\n39: #\n40: # Included files, as well as files pointed to by java.security.properties,\n41: # can include other files recursively. Paths may be absolute or relative.\n42: # Each relative path is resolved against the base file containing its\n43: # \"include\" definition, if local. Paths may contain system properties for\n44: # expansion in the form of ${system.property}. If a system property does\n45: # not have a value, it expands to the empty string.\n46: #\n47: # An error will be thrown if a file cannot be included. This may happen\n48: # if the file cannot be resolved, does not exist, is a directory, there are\n49: # insufficient permissions to read it, it is recursively included more than\n50: # once, or for any other reason. The order is 1-based; 1 is the most preferred, followed\n77: # by 2, and so on.\n78: #\n79: # <provName> must specify the name of the Provider as passed to its super\n80: # class java.security.Provider constructor. This is for providers loaded\n81: # through the ServiceLoader mechanism.\n82: #\n83: # <className> must specify the subclass of the Provider class whose\n84: # constructor sets the values of various properties that are required\n85: # for the Java Security API to look up the algorithms or other\n86: # facilities implemented by the provider.
